# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes RBAC ClusterRole Verb Coverage Audit

## Your Task

Audit kubernetes/kubernetes for completeness of RBAC verb handling. Find all Go source files that define the set of allowed verbs (get, list, watch, create, update, patch, delete, deletecollection) and validate that all API handlers enforce these verb constraints.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the compliance domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive audit of Kubernetes v1.32.0 for RBAC verb coverage. Here's what I found:

## Summary of Findings

I've created `/workspace/answer.json` with a detailed audit documenting:

### **19 Key Files** that define or enforce verb handling:
- **OpenAPI verb registry**: Defines validation for operation IDs
- **Endpoint installer**: Maps HTTP verbs to Kubernetes verbs for discovery
- **RBAC bootstrap policy**: Defines semantic verb groups (Write, ReadWrite, Read, ReadUpdate)
- **kubectl create role**: Validates allowed verbs
- **Request parser**: Identifies special verbs and selector-enabled verbs
- **CRD discovery controller**: Defines verbs for custom resources
- **Authorization filters**: Enforces verb constraints
- **Controllers** (namespace deletion, resource quota, garbage collection): Validate verb support before operations

### **16 Key Symbols** that define verb sets:
- `verbs` (Trie in OpenAPI)
- `toDiscoveryKubeVerb` (HTTP→Kube mapping)
- `Write`, `ReadWrite`, `Read`, `ReadUpdate` (verb groups)
- `validResourceVerbs`, `specialVerbs`, `verbsWithSelectors`
- `SupportsAllVerbs` (discovery predicate)
- `resourceVerbs` (kubectl auth)
- `Attributes`, `APIResource` (core interfaces)

### **Coverage Chain** showing enforcement flow:
1. `WithAuthorization` (authorization filter)
2. `DeleteResource` (delete handler)
3. `registerResourceHandlers` (HTTP binding)
4. `ConvertGroupVersionIntoToDiscovery` (discovery generation)

The audit confirms **comprehensive verb coverage** across all eight standard verbs (get, list, watch, create, update, patch, delete, deletecollection) with proper enforcement at the authorization, handler, and controller layers.

Custom Resource Definition Discovery** (staging/src/k8s.io/apiextensions-apiserver/pkg/apiserver/customresource_discovery_controller.go:141, 144)\\nDefines two verb sets for CRD resources:\\n- Normal: [delete, deletecollection, get, list, patch, create, update, watch]\\n- Terminating: [delete, deletecollection, get, list, watch]\\n\\n**7. kubectl auth can-i Verb Set** (staging/src/k8s.io/kubectl/pkg/cmd/auth/cani.go:108)\\nDefines resourceVerbs for authorization checking: [get, list, watch, create, update, patch, delete, deletecollection, use, bind, impersonate, *, approve, sign, escalate, attest]\\n\\n### Verb Validation Points\\n\\n**1. RBAC Policy Rule Validation** (pkg/apis/rbac/helpers.go:186-200)\\nThe PolicyRuleBuilder.Rule() method enforces that when ResourceNames are specified, certain verbs (list, watch, create, deletecollection) cannot be used, as they operate on collections rather than specific resources.\\n\\n**2. Authorization Filter** (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authorization.go)\\nThe WithAuthorization handler extracts verb from RequestInfo and passes it to the authorizer for decision-making.\\n\\n**3. API Handler Registration** (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/installer.go:registerResourceHandlers)\\nRegisters HTTP handlers for each action verb, mapping storage capabilities to supported operations.\\n\\n**4. Resource Deletion Controllers** (pkg/controller/namespace/deletion/namespaced_resources_deleter.go, pkg/controller/garbagecollector/garbagecollector.go)\\nValidate that resources support required verbs (delete, deletecollection) before attempting operations.\\n\\n**5. Resource Quota Controller** (pkg/controller/resourcequota/resource_quota_controller.go:559)\\nFilters resources to only those supporting [create, list, watch, delete] verbs for quota enforcement.\\n\\n**6. CRD Handler** (staging/src/k8s.io/apiextensions-apiserver/pkg/apiserver/customresource_handler.go)\\nManages HTTP handlers for CRD resources, respecting the verb sets defined in the discovery controller.\\n\\n### Key Enforcement Mechanisms\\n\\n1. **Authorization Attributes Interface** (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/authorizer/interfaces.go:34)\\nThe Attributes.GetVerb() method documents supported verbs: get, list, watch, create, update, patch, delete, deletecollection, proxy.\\n\\n2. **APIResource Verbs Field** (staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/apis/meta/v1/types.go:1203-1205)\\nAll API resources expose a Verbs list in discovery, enabling clients to determine supported operations.\\n\\n3. **Discovery Helper** (staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/discovery/helper.go:139-146)\\nThe SupportsAllVerbs predicate enables filtering resources by verb support, used throughout controllers.\\n\\n4. **Metrics Verb Normalization** (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/metrics/metrics.go:700-733)\\nThe CanonicalVerb function normalizes verbs for metrics collection (e.g., distinguishing LIST from GET, normalizing WATCHLIST to WATCH).\\n\\n### Coverage Assessment\\n\\nThe audit confirms that Kubernetes v1.32.0 has comprehensive verb coverage across multiple layers:\\n\\n- **Verb Definition**: Centralized definitions in openapi, bootstrap policies, CLI tools, and request parsing\\n- **Verb Mapping**: Clear HTTP-to-Kube verb translation in the installer\\n- **Verb Validation**: RBAC rules enforce semantic constraints (e.g., no list/watch on named resources)\\n- **Verb Enforcement**: Authorization filters apply verb constraints before handler execution\\n- **Verb Discovery**: All API delete, deletecollection) are consistently defined across the codebase with proper enforcement at authorization, handler, and controller layers.\"\n}\n",
